text:
I made this 1 other time before and followed the recipe to a T. It was very good and the proportions are very balanced. This time I made sure to cut the celery and carrot pieces smaller than the onion so that they are all done at the same time. I also substituted some half-and-half for the chicken broth (1/4 of the portion) just to give it some richness and color. I added about 3/4 tbsp. of poultry seasoning and a dash of cayenne. I used frozen peas instead of canned and did not bake the biscuits with the casserole. I used frozen buttermilk biscuits and poured the mixture on top. I love the way that the biscuit melts when the sauce is poured on it. This time it came out DIVINE.

This is a staple wintertime recipe.  Also, hate to say it, but I've made it both with chicken broth and then with 4 bouillon cubes + 4 cups water.  Now I like to go "fresh" when I can, but it was much blander with the chick. broth.  Tastes considerably better with the bouillon cubes; either way, it's an excellent recipe, and nice to see a casserole without a can of soup in it, and also with so many fresh veggies.

text:
UPDATE: Try this recipe with mashed potoatoes on top in lieu of the biscuits called for (i.e. like a chicken shepherd's pie).  I got this idea from Rachel Ray.  All in all, I prefer this better as is (i.e. with a biscuit crust), but had to give it a try...  This is an excellent recipe!!!  My friend who has the "favorites" cookbook recommended it to me (it's in the original paperback).  I do not like the "crust" part of pot pies, but I love the filling, so this recipe is perfect for me! The biscuits are just yummy!  I made this casserole for my parents and they loved it too!  I added some fresh mushrooms, pearl onions and a little cookig sherry (you could also use white wine...) to make it extra special :) I made more than 8 biscuits (8 didn't seem to be enough to cover the entire 9x13 pan) and didn't flatten them as the recipe directed (I just spooned heaping mounds of biscuit mix onto the filling). This dish pairs nicely with a tossed salad.  I'll definitely make this again. It's a keeper! Thanks for sharing!!!

text:
I made the chicken mixture according to the recipe, except I added a little poultry seasoning.  It was very good but next time I make this I'll use frozen peas instead of canned.  Some other reviews had mentioned there needed to be more biscuits so I used 3 cups Bisquit, 2 cups milk and two teaspoons basil. It made 12 good sized biscuits that covered the whole pan.  I didn't roll them as the recipe stated, I just did drop biscuits.  This was very good and will definately be made again. However, we had leftover since there's only two of us and the leftovers were not great, the biscuits soaked up the broth and it was just kinda dry, so I would suggest cutting the recipe in half, using a 9x9 inch pan if you're only making it for two people.

Soooooo very good! I didn't add the celery, but I did add corn and potatoes (that I cooked in the microwave first). I also used 4 chicken stock cubes and 4 cups of water instead of the chicken broth. I didn't roll or flatten the biscuits with my hands as the instructions stated to do. I realized that my biscuit mix was much too sticky to mess with so instead I just spooned 6 "blops" of the mix onto the chicken mixture. Then I cooked the whole thing in a round casserole dish instead of the 9 X 13 inch baking dish.

OMG,these are so awesome!  I just served them for dinner and there's absolutely no leftovers.  Everyone went for seconds and kept on raving about how great it was. I had no peas, so I used frozen shelled edamame - delicious!  As far as leftovers, I used the same technique as I use with leftover matzoh ball soup, that is, to remove the biscuits from the leftover casserole and store them separately, then reunite them with the casserole when it's time to reheat for another meal.  I will be making this often!

text:
I would give this seven stars. wow, so easy and so delicious. I agree with the frozen peas over canned and chopping the carrots smaller to cook evenly with onions. I didn't have celery, so I just subbed in more onion- I had lots of small sweet onions on hand, tasted great, not bland at all. I also used chopped fresh basil, but maybe with fresh you have to add more, because I barely noticed it, and I love basil. Also, I didn't use baking mix, but opted for the E-Z drop biscuit recipe from this site, and carefully spooned it onto the filling-nearly covered whole whole pan. It really filled up my 9x13 pan, to the brim, I was worried the biscuits would make it overflow, but only a little bubbled out. Definitely halve if made for two or three.  We had friends for lunch (the main meal in Spain), and still had leftovers for dinner for everyone (me, hubby, two kids-1&3)
This was delicious, and so easy, especially with my Thermomix (wedding present) to do all the chopping and stirring and boiling of the filling for me.  The biscuits did not soak up anymore filling in the tupper, they got chicken and veggies stuck to them, which seemed to act as a slight barrier.  I really cannot say enough good things about this recipe. And so glad it just uses chicken broth, not cream of anything- they don't have Campbells in Spain yet.

text:
this is a good base to start with, i love lots of flavor and i knew this would be bland so i added to it like others have. first, i did sautee the onions, garlic and celery until softened then i added 3/4 bag of frozen mixed vegies. i added poultry seasoning, salt, pepper, cayenne and italian spices to taste. as others recommended i too used canned biscuits. you may want to cook them a bit (not completely) first according to directions then add them to the casserole towards the end of cooking. i didn't want to cook them entirely independently, because i really wanted the biscuits to suck up more flavor and juices from the casserole. a good recipe it does need more flavor, basil alone just isn't enough.

text:
I do a much easier and quicker version of this using canned veggies-drained, 1 can each: sweet peas, coined carrots and mixed veggies ("Veg-All" type, the ones with the limas in it not the ones with potatoes), 1 large can of cream of chicken soup and 1/2 a bag of frozen cubed hashbrown potatoes. Top it  with refrigerated canned biscuits (the "grands"-style, the buttery flaky ones work well) and all you need to do is cook it long enough to brown the biscuits in the oven! I even start with raw chicken and brown it with the onions and celery (and hash browns) and it still only takes 30 minutes start to finish! it is delicious! And I use sage or poultry seasoning rather than basil-no need for salt. (LOL I rate mine 5 stars...)

text:
A good recipe that I did modify a bit.  In preparing the 2nd step of the recipe, I cooked off the vegetables in the butter. In a separate bowl I mixed the flour, salt, pepper, basil and a teaspoon of Thyme, omitting the sugar.  I then tossed the diced uncooked chicken in the flour mixture, added to the cooking vegetables and cooked together for approximately five minutes.  I've found that this keeps the chicken tender and mingles the flavors nicely.  Add in the broth with a Tablespoon of worcestershire sauce and a few dashes of Tabasco.  Bring to a boil, then lower to a simmer and added in a cup of sliced white mushrooms and the canned peas.  I doubled the biscuits for the size of the pan and to keep my wife from stealing mine.   A good dish that was enjoyed by the whole family.

text:
This recipe was  very easy to make and delicious. Obviously, not everyone will have the same spice and/or vegetable preferences, but it's so easy to use this basic recipe and swap out the specifics to suit your family's tastes.  For my family, I went a little easy on the basil and added our favorite poultry seasoning.  Just be sure to taste the chicken mixture before you pour it into the prepared baking dish.  If it needs a little more flavor, add whatever suits you. Since I am gluten free, I used my own GF allpurpose flour in the chicken mixture, and gluten free cheddar biscuts (the recipe is on the Betty Crocker website.)  It was ready to take from the oven after the initial 30 minutes.  That may vary depending on the biscuits you choose to use.  Our biscuits were done to perfection w/o the additional ten minutes of bake time.

text:
This was an excellent way to use up my leftover turkey and would work great with leftover chicken as well. I only made a couple minor changes: per previous reviewers advice, I used 3 cps chicken broth and 1 cup half-and-half. I left out the salt, enough in the chicken broth. I used Bisquik and milk I soured (put 1 Tpsb vinegar or lemon juice in a measuring cup, fill to the one cup line with milk. Let sit for 5-10 minutes, will look curdled, stir and use desired amount. This is a substitute for buttermilk). I just did drop biscuits on top of the chicken mixture. Canned peas tasted fine but are not as fresh looking as frozen. Everyone ate it up. Next time, I will use double the veggies and less chicken. Great recipe, thanks!

I couldn't wait to try this recipe and much to my disappointment, I couldn't find any chicken in the freezer. So I made it with leftover cut up tri-tip steaks and beef broth. I also didn't have peas so I threw in a couple cups of chopped, steamed broccoli. I made the biscuits from scratch and mixed in a little basil for flavor and this is really a good recipe. Over all a great recipe though.

I read many of the reviews and got a kick out of the range - "loved it" to "would never make it again".  As a cook, I enjoy tinkering with a recipe.  Rarely do I follow the exact list or amount in a recipe (with the exception of deserts, which demand precision).  This casserole dish was an excellent base.  It gave me a starting point which I might not have thought of on my own.  I boosted the onion and garlic to my family's taste, added fresh parsley and cilantro to the soup base, used frozen peas and corn, added thyme and rosemary while cutting the basil.  It worked!  My picky wife and daughter enjoyed it and I had seconds.  Preparation is a bit more than 30 minutes. Start to finish took 90 minutes.

text:
This was lovely, I would certainly make it again. It is time consuming, so don't come home at 6pm from work and want to eat by 7, not going to happen.
I was having a bit of prob getting the flour to thicken and it lumped up, but a whisk sorted it right out. 
The only change I would make  next time would be to eliminate the sugar as I could taste it and it isn't necessary. I didn't have canned peas so used frozen mixed carrots and peas, was lovely. I also didn't have buttermilk mix, so used regular bisquick and was great. Enough to make 2 meals for 2 people.

I have also used left over beef for this recipe and it is just as good as the chicken. After making this numerous times there are a few short cuts to make dinner a bit quicker. I eliminate the butter completely and when cooking the chicken you can add the onions and garlic, salt and pepper then. Then remove the chicken from the pan briefly. I also add the flour and basil to the broth and whisk it all together in a pitcher, then add it to the celery/onion/garlic in the pan with carrots...let simmer then add rest of veg, again simmer then put chicken back in...less lumps in the flour mixture if you add it together then add to pan...

Excellent!  I was so excited to find a chicken pot pie/biscuits recipe that did not call for condensed soup (yuck!)!  Made this for dinner last night pretty much following recipe as written.  Omitted celery (none on hand), added mushroom and diced red potatoes (pre cooked in the microwave), used fresh peas and doubled the garlic. Easy peasy although it takes a little more effort than a dump and bake recipe but well worth the effort!  Tastes great!

I cook very often and I enjoy making everything from scratch so this appealed to me. I followed the recipe but always add my own herbs if I think there isn't going to be enough flavor. This was very good, very, very filling, my husband who can eat (and is thin of course, men lol) could only eat two biscuits worth. I followed measurements but only had two cups of chopped chicken and it worked out just fine. I added Rosemary, Parsley and a bit more Basil (fresh) and it was very flavorful. This is a bit too much pepper for me so I'm glad I omitted the 1/8 of teaspoon I left out, if you don't like pepper you want to cut it in half. I found this to be a very good winter supper. It is time consuming, not difficult but takes a lot of prep but as does any good home cooked meal. I used Pillsbury Buttermilk Biscuits instead of making my own, there were just enough to cover my pan on top. I feel like is too many biscuits for the chicken mixture, my husband had two and myself one and half the mixture is gone so I will reduce biscuits next time. Overall, I will try this again, adding less biscuits, but other then that the flavor is spot on, no bland chicken and biscuits here, kudos to the writer this is one of the few (if any) recipes that I have not had to seriously alter I would definitely recommend this.

text:
So easy, good, and hearty! I used frozen vegetables, frozen bisquits (Grands) and Publix's rotisserie chicken. 4 cups was the entire chicken. By the time the bisquits were done (20-25 min) the chicken mixture/gravy was done; perfect timing! This is better than chicken pot pie because you get the extra dough from the biscuits. It's also nice because you only need to cook the # of biscuits that you will eat at that meal so they don't get soggy. Tomorrow for lunch I'll pop a couple more biscuits in the oven, heat up the chicken mixure and have a great lunch! Also, the mixture can be frozen! Another reason to give this a try ... you don't have to throw away left overs. BTW .. you do need to like basil; the taste definitely comes through

text:
Overall, this is a hearty, simple, and very tasty recipe. I poached my chicken to cook it quickly, and two large boneless breasts seemed to be just enough. 

As someone else mentioned, it is a lot of food for just two, and I agree that I would cut the recipe in half and use a 9x9 baking dish. 

Instead of making the biscuits I used pre-packaged home-style buttermilk biscuits, and they worked great! 

Also, the bottom of the biscuits don't get crispy because they soak up the moisture from the chicken mixture. I prefer mine crispier, so next time I would save some biscuits and bake them aside from the mixture and just spoon some on top.

text:
Oh so good.  While I think the recipe is fine on its own, I customized with the following: chopped the onion/celery/carrots in the food processor, then cooked with about 1.5lbs of chopped chicken breast.  Used a 12oz can of evaporated milk and 2.5C of chicken broth for the liquid.  Also added additional spices/herbs to our taste.  Substituted honey for sugar (in our house, everything is better with honey in it!).  Since I prefer 'from-scratch', cut 1/2C butter into 2C self-rising flour (food processor works great for this too), then mixed in 1/4C apple cider (since it's fall) and 1/2C buttermilk, with only 1t of the basil, which made a great biscuit topping. Loved, loved, loved it.

I was in the mood for chicken pot pie, but didn't have the time to make the pie shell.  Found this recipe and I don't think I will be making chix pot pie again!  I pretty much stuck to the recipe as it was written, but used less peas.  Also, instead of the buttermilk baking mix, I used the E-Z Drop Biscuits recipe from this site.  While I am cooking the garlic and onion, I cook chicken strips that I have seasoned with salt and pepper and EVOO in the toaster-oven set at 375 f for about 10-15 mins..  They cook very quickly.  The baking dish I use also fits very nicely in the toaster-oven.   Will be our regular Wednesday Night Chicken night on the cold winter months ahead.  Very hearty, great comfort food.  And, best of all, it feeds my large family!  I can't please all the kids, but when it's 4 out of 5, I couldn't be happier!  Husband loves it too!

AWESOME!  I did this as a stew served over the biscuits.  It was a little too thin so I thickened it with a flour/milk (or you could use water) mixture.  I also cooked the chicken in the pan and removed it before sauteing the veggies - a little more of the chicken flavor.   Overall this recipe is a big improvement on our old family favorite made with condensed cream of chicken soup, and I will be making it again!

Continued. . .I've made this so many times now.  Definitely a go to recipe.  Still haven't baked it as a casserole - always serve it over biscuits.  I usually add a bunch of vegetables including carrots, beans, corn, potatoes, and pureed zucchini.  Also have done it in the crock pot - cook chicken for a few hours till it pulls apart, then add everything else and let cook till veggies are no longer crunchy.  So much flavor.  So yummy!!

I was hoping for leftovers so I didn't have to cook the next day but there weren't any. I sauted in olive oil instead of butter. I don't care for celery so I used a combination of frozen peas, carrots and corn. I didn't have any fresh garlic so I sprinkled in a little bit of garlic salt. I estimated the spices and it turned out fine. The sauce turned out thick not runny which is how I like it. For the biscuits I used the fluffy whole wheat recipe from this site and forgot to add in basil. I also used another reviewers suggestion and I cooked the biscuits separately and spooned the mixture on top instead of cooking in the oven. I was hungry and didn't want to wait 40 minutes.

This was great! Dh called it perfect comfort food. I followed the recipe exactly, except I cheated and used a can of 10 biscuits. Next time dh asked me to use 2 cans. I also poached the chicken the day before, and used the resulting broth in the recipe as well. Just boiled some water in a large pot with a quartered onion and some crushed garlic cloves. Added the chicken breasts, partly covered the pot, and simmered for about 10 minutes. The chicken shreds up really easily then, and the broth is light and perfect fot casseroles like this one. We will definately make this again!

I MADE A FEW SUBSTITUTIONS TO REDUCE FAT, AND EASE PREPARATION.  I USED FROZEN CUT CARROTS, AND PURDUE "SHORT CUTS" ROASTED CHICKEN (2 PACKS.)  I USED 2 CUPS OF WINE AND 2 CUPS OF BROTH (INSTEAD OF 4 CUPS BROTH), AND I JUST USED ABOUT A TABLESPOON OF BUTTER (INSTEAD OF 1/4 CUP) TO SAUTEE VEGGIES.  I ADDED THE FLOUR SLOWLY, AND ADDED BROTH A LITTLE AT A TIME WITH THE FLOUR TO KEEP IT FROM CLUMPING.  I USED THE REDUCED FAT BISQUIK MIX, AND ADDED ABOUT 2 TABLESPOON PARMESAN CHEESE, INSTEAD OF THE BASIL.  THE CASSEROLE TURNED OUT GREAT, AND IT WAS SO EASY TO MAKE !!  IT IS DEFINITLEY A "KEEPER."  MY HUSBAND, WHO OPTS FOR HOT, SPICY FOOD ANYTIME, EVEN LOVED IT.  CAN'T WAIT TO MAKE IT FOR FRIENDS AND FAMILY.  IT'S EVEN BETTER THE NEXT DAY, IF YOU HAVE LEFTOVERS.

text:
I have made this several times, with various changes each time as I like to experiment, but the base recipe is a solid recipe for chicken and biscuit casserole.

I always find that rosemary or basil and rosemary both tends to result in a more fragrant meal, and I especially like to put it in the biscuits--don't skimp on it, either, as it really does tie the meal together. Give this recipe a try, you won't regret it.

For a less dish-intensive way to make the recipe, use an electric high-sided skillet to cook the casserole part and bake the biscuits on a foil-lined pan in the oven; this ensures your biscuits don't get mushy, even for the leftovers, and means you only have one cooking pan to clean.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I found this recipe doing an ingredients search for chicken, basil, and carrots so right off the bat I was going to modify it to whatever I had on hand. I had a lot of fresh green beans and I substituted those for the canned/frozen peas. I also like things a tad spicy so I made a dry rub for my chicken, which was cooked in a NuWave. The dry rub was 1/2 tsp salt, 1/2 tsp pepper, 1/4 tsp cayenne pepper, and 1/2 tsp sesame seeds. I sprinkled the dry rub on each side of the chicken tenders prior to cooking. In my veggie mix I had sweet onion, carrots, celery, and green beans, all chopped to bite size. I sauteed them in butter for a bit, then added chicken broth to cover them and a bouillon chicken cube to add flavor based on previous reviewer comments. I then added a little less than 1/3 cup of flour - my goal was to have the sauce thicken but still be a bit soupy. The major sub I made was corn bread for the biscuits, which came out absolutely amazing since corn bread was a little sweet and mixed very well with the spicy chicken profile. For that I used a package of corn bread muffin mix with egg and milk and then spread the mixture over my casserole dish containing the veggies and cut up chicken mix. I baked that in the over for 30 minutes at 350 and the meal came out phenomenal. Corn bread did not get soggy at all for lunch the next day!

text:
Sooooo good!  Chicken pot pie is one of our favorites, but putting it in a 13 x 9 dish appealed to me, since I'm feeding teenaged boys.  I like the biscuits; I followed the recipe (using just scant tsp basil, and less milk so they formed a good dough) and flattened them a lot.  I was in a hurry, so thin as they were, the casserole was done in about 25 minutes, without the 10 extra minutes covered in foil.  Next time I may double the biscuit dough, make em thicker.  I probably used a bit more than 1/2 cup ea of the onion, celery & carrots, then I used about a cup each of frozen peas and frozen cut green beans.  I substituted 1 tsp herbes de provence seasoning blend for the basil in the filling since other reviewers said the basil was overpowering, plus it's my favorite seasoning for chicken.  The filling was so rich and delicious!  I just polished off the last small portion for lunch (after hiding it from the boys), and I think I may reduce or even eliminate the salt next time.  I use Wolfgang Puck roasted chicken broth and there is plenty of flavor w/o added salt.  Definitely a keeper, unanimous in my family!

OK... I made this recipe, which was a lot of work but totally worth it.  We ended up eating it for 3 nights in a row until it was gone. text:
This recipe is fabulous and a 'must-try' for every cook.  I did customize to our liking and convenience though.  I used: 
2 cans of Swanson's Chicken Broth (14-1/2 oz. size) 
plus added 1/2 cup milk after I thickened the the veggies and broth in step 2.  
I used frozen peas 
and 
a whole rotisserie chicken plus the juices in the packaging, minus any fat, skin and bones. 
  
For the biscuits I used:
2-1/3 cups bisquick mix and cut the basil in half.
In the oven for 35 minutes
raised oven temp to 400 removed foil and browned my biscuits perfectly.
After my changes it was definately a 5 star  meal.

Great recipe! After using other people's suggestions, adding 3/4 Tbsp. poultry seasoning, 4 bouillion cubes and 4 cups of water instead of chicken broth and frozen peas instead of canned, I used cornbread instead of biscuit mix.  Make a regular cornbread recipe off the box and plop it onto the top of the mixed casserole about three across.  Bake for 25 minutes instead of 40 and serve as suggested. My three men loved it and we didn't have any leftovers.  I will definately make this again.  Great way to use up leftover chicken.

text:
My family enjoyed this but there wasn't a mad rush for leftovers. We made it a bit more healthy by doubling up on the veggies, using frozen peas instead of canned (less sodium), fat free low sodium broth and then fat free half and half to bring the two cans of broth up to the 4 cup line. We sauteed the veggies in smart balance butter flavored spread (lite) and I used low fat bisquick for the veggies. I also omitted the basil and added 1 tsp of poultry seasoning to the flour mixture and added garlic powder rather than basil to the biscuits. I think that biscuits from scratch probably would've been better but this was a decently fast, healthy meal overall.

This recipe definitely deserves 5 stars.  I followed it pretty much as written.  I used darker meat chicken and the broth from it.  I have found that the darker meat makes for more flavor. I used 3 cups broth and 1 cup half and half for a creamier taste.  I made biscuits from my favorite recipe and used coconut oil in the biscuits. My chicken and biscuit recipe from now on!!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This recipe was a great starting point. I used this recipe and a combination of tips from comments to make my dish. For the chicken in this recipe, I bought a store-made rotisserie chicken and picked and shredded the meat. In place of the water/milk, I used two cans of Campbell's cream of chicken with mushroom soup. For the veggies, I used all fresh (no canned) vegetables. I cooked 3/4 cup each of onion, peas, string beans, mushroom, and corn in a saucepan with about 2 tbls of minced garlic. I added 2 pinches each of basil and rosemary. For the biscuits, I used the pre-made mix for the Red Lobster Brand Cheddar biscuits. I cooked in the oven for 30 mins. at 400 degrees. With about 3 minutes left, I poured the garlic/butter sauce that came in the biscuit box on top and let it finish. Tasted amazing! I precut and froze all my extra veggies, so I will have an easy time making it again.

I followed the recipe pretty closely, but I did the biscuits differently.  I had a box of Red Lobster Cheddar Bay biscuit mix in the pantry, so I made those as per the package directions.  I made the chicken mixture using water and bouillon because another reviewer mentioned that it was more flavorful than using broth.  I also used frozen peas that I had in the freezer.  I made the chicken mixture early in the afternoon, covered and refrigerated it.  I left it covered while reheating and baked the biscuits separately.  I served this with the biscuits on the side, along with a simple green salad.  The only change I would make next time is to bump up the veggies, maybe by half.  One thing I really like about this recipe is that its made with ingredients I normally have on hand.  This will be repeated again soon!  Thanks, CVERNSMITH, for the recipe!

text:
This was basically an okay recipe, but I found I needed to tweek it too much for it to be considered 5-star. I used frozen peas, not canned (I hate canned peas!) I cut the sugar in half, and included about 1 cup of diced potatoes in with the vegetables and butter.. After adding the seasonings (basil, salt and pepper) to the sauce, I found that it really needed more flavor. I added some dried parsley, marjoram, cayenne, thyme and sage (I did not measure; just to taste).  I did not add the basil to the biscuit dough. Instead I folded in about 1/2 cup of shredded cheddar, brushing the biscuits with melted butter about 15 minutes into the baking process. These changes elevated it to a more flavorful dish. Still don't know if it was a 5, but it was good.

text:
I have made this as is and I've made it with a few tweaks. It is good both ways, but for a quicker meal, I use the following tweaks. If you want to save a bit of chopping and won't miss the celery, you can add a bag of frozen mixed veggies (corn, carrots, peas, and green beans). Omit the carrots and celery in the beginning. Cook the veggies according to the package and add when the recipes call for the peas. As for the biscuits, I do follow the recipe for making them, but do them as a drop biscuit instead. I just drop 10-12 smaller biscuits in the pan on top of the chicken/veggies. It works great with less mess. Just try to keep the biscuits as even in size as possible so they cook evenly. This is a favorite in my house, even with my picky-eater husband and five year-old daughter!

country:

text:
This was very simple to make and had a good flavor- I added additional chicken bouillon to match my families taste, but it was good enough as it was.  The ONLY major issue I found was the density/texture of the biscuits.  While we enjoyed finally getting biscuits that would cook through, and did not turn to mush in the pan, they were excessively dry and required saturation with the sauce.  Even then, when fully "doused", they were dry if made exactly as per recipe.  I will make this again because I like the taste and ease of preparation, but I will have to try an alternative version of the biscuits.  Another side note: the amount of peas added to the sauce can cause it to turn an unappetizing green color.  Be sparing in the amount added and avoid the "baby" peas, which seem to be the ones that crush and release color too easily.  All in all though, good job!

I loved it! I used Better Than Bouillion for the broth, so next time I would cut the added salt down to maybe 1/2 tsp or maybe no added salt, as it was a bit too salty for my taste. Used about a cup of frozen peas that I added during the simmering time plus a little dry sherry for added flavor, then just plopped spoonfuls of Bisquick biscuit dough I mixed up w/o basil as it is a bit strong for the kids' taste. text:
Yum! and easy to make. Followed a few recommendations from the other helpful reviewers, thanks:

1) I cut recipe in half because I'm cooking for 2 people (and we still had half the volume for leftovers).

2) I used frozen peas (bought Birds Eye "singles" packs and used only 1/2 that portion bag -- or whatever matches volume of other veggies).

3) For the chicken broth: I used half broth, half milk.

4) For the biscuits: 
--Made the full volume of mix (did not half that portion since most reviewers thought the full volume recipe didn't have enough biscuit).
--I used regular Bisquick blended with buttermilk (could have used a little more buttermilk, for a slightly moister biscuit).
--Just spooned biscuit mix onto the casserole; a little more than 1/8 cup per biscuit. This filled out perfectly in an 9x9 stone dish.

5) The dried basil spice was great; not overwhelming in the least; subtle but nice flavor (one reviewer thought it would be easy to overdo this spice...it wasn't a strong flavor so i can't agree).

Followed the same cooking time. Everything turned out great. My husband enjoyed it too. It's a keeper!

This was a really great recipe!  I highly suggest trying it!  I only did a few things differently.  First, I did not want to use packaged Bisquick.  I used The Pioneer Woman's drop biscuit recipe that goes with her sausage gravy recipe.  I added the dried basil to that.  The biscuits were tender and flavorful.  I added more chicken than called for.  I used a rotisserie chicken from the grocery store.  This made it so easy!  I added a few more seasonings to the gravy/sauce according to some recommendations from other reviewers.  I added poultry seasoning and parsley.  Also, another reviewer suggested subbing some milk for some of the chicken broth. I used 1 c milk and 3 c chicken broth.  This was a winner!

text:
Yes I will make it again, I thought it was very tasty.  I did however make a couple of changes:  instead of adding any sugar I cooked one cob of corn, cut corn off the cob and added it instead of the sugar for sweetness and it was just perfect.  Also, I added only 1 tsp. of dried basil to biscuit mix instead of 2 (thank goodness!).  I think 2 would have been too overpowering considering there is also some in the chicken mixture.  Be careful when adding salt depending on what kind of chicken broth you use, I could see this being a bit on the salty side if not careful.  Also, I did not cover casserole with foil the last 10 minutes at all because my biscuits needed to cook just a bit more.  It really was delicious!

A little bit too peppery for me, but my family really enjoyed this - it's made its way into my handwritten recipe box at their request. I made this recipe with chicken bullion instead of broth and seasoned the chicken with poultry rub before I baked it for added flavor.  Otherwise, the only change I made was to substitute mashed potatoes for the biscuits (a great way to use up leftovers). A bag of shredded cheese on the table to sprinkle on top if desired completed the meal to rave reviews. It took a little longer to make than I anticipated,  but that's often the case when I try a new recipe. I'm sure I'll speed up as I make it more often. Hopefully next time I will be able to try it with the biscuits. I also really like the fact that this dish doesn't involve dumping a can of "cream of something" soup into it to make a thick, flavorful sauce/filling. I have quite enough of those types of recipes already. Excellent dish!

I have tried this recipe twice now.  Very good!  I think baking the chicken in the oven yourself is the best way to prepare the cooked chicken.  Rub oil, salt and pepper on 2 to 3 chicken breasts (skin on, bone in). Place on silicone baking sheet on baking pan.  Bake at 400 degrees for 25 to 40 minutes (until thoroughly cooked).  Remove pan from oven and let cool.  Skin slides right off, then you can hand-pull bite size pieces of chicken to use in this recipe.

text:
this was a good basic recipe. It can be used as a base for other dishes, such as chicken a la king, chicken pot pie. I made it without the sugar,  Instead of adding dried basil, I used a Tuscan flavored broth infused with thyme, basil and rosemary. The seasonings were subtle but improved the flavor. I skipped the biscuit topping and served it with a side of mashed potatoes seasoned with salt, pepper and fresh grated nutmeg. I also mashed them with butter and heavy cream. It was a nice, easy comfort food meal for a rainy night. Next time I may make this as a chicken pot pie adding some mushrooms and diced potatoes.

text:
This was REALLY good. However, I should note that I went with another reviewer's suggestion of using a cup of half & half (1/4 of the broth ingredient) to 3 cups chicken broth. Made it rich and creamy, which is the way I like this kind of dish. I noticed another reviewer's comment that her biscuits soaked up all of the 'gravy' but also noticed that she said she used drop biscuits. I would like to point out that using drop biscuits *will* soak up the gravy, which is possibly why this recipe suggests rolled biscuits instead. I would go with the biscuits the recipe states or make your biscuits separate rather than baking them with the chicken mixture. This would also be great over mashed potatoes or toast.

text:
I altered the recipe based on what was in my pantry.  I used 2 boneless chicken breasts and covered them with a lid when I cooked them to contain the moisture, which I then substituted for part of the chicken broth.  I didn't have peas or onions so I doubled both the celery and the carrots and added onion powder when I mixed in the flour.  I used half the butter and added it in slowly so it wouldn't cook away.  I only used 1/4 cup of flour and 1 3/4 cup chicken broth.  I added 1/4 cup white wine.  I did not use any sugar.  I halved the dough recipe, and because I hate how sticky it gets, I just dropped it on top like little drop biscuits.  I added some crumbled Ritz crackers on top for a little extra crunchiness, although I am not sure that they made that much of a difference.  I cooked it uncovered for 30 minutes at 350 in a slightly smaller casserole dish.  I am not sure how my version compares with the original, but my husband and I really enjoyed it.  I give the recipe five stars just because it was so flexible and turned out so well in spite of my alterations.

text:
This is a great recipe! Thank you for sharing!
I made some changes based on reviews, I cooked three chicken breast halves in 4.5 cups of water to which I added 4 bullion cubes, onion, celery and a bag of frozen mixed vegetables once boiling. I took the chicken breasts out once cooked through, let them cool a little while and shredded them. I then sauteed more onions, fresh minced garlic and green peppers in the butter, once cooked I added the flour and then mixed it all into the broth from the chicken with the vegetables and added the chicken, mixed it all up and put it in a round casserole dish and topped it off with a can of refrigerated biscuits. It was absolutely amazing, the kids loved it and requested that I make it again!

Easy AND delicious, and I keep these ingredients on hand.  I cut the recipe in half since I wasn't cooking for a crowd.  I substituted Mrs. Dash and Green Beans because I was out of basil and peas.  I even used a heart-healthy baking mix- I just dropped it over the top instead of shaping actual biscuits. I cut down the cook times by a few minutes because of the smaller portion. Really good casserole.  I also added poultry seasoning and used heavy cream and 2 small potatoes to thicken it up a bit.  I did not use flour.  I used cornstarch instead.   I did not add any sugar .  All in all it was very good.   Next time I will not add basil to the dumplings.  I found the basil too overpowering.**EDIT** Made again on 3/15/11 ~ Made this on the stove top did not put into oven at all. I used leftovers from a roasted chicken I made a couple of nights ago.  Took all the meat off the bones and chopped up and threw into the pot.  The additional flavors from the roasted chicken really add a nice level of flavor to the whole meal. Also, I used a dumpling recipe from the Bisquick box and topped the chicken stew with those instead of baking biscuits in the oven. Really preferred it this way.  Again I did not add any sugar and added a bit more broth as to make it soupier. Still very good blend of ingredients and sooo comforting on a cold winters day. Thanks Again !!!

text:
This is an excellent family dinner.  A great way to use up left-over Thanksgiving turkey and aging vegetables.  My kids love it!  UPDATE: I've made this with bouillion and with freshly made chicken stock. No surprise that the stock "made" the dish. Also, I omit the basil in the biscuits and in the stew, use frozen peas, and add a generous amount of poultry seasoning. I put this is a deep, round casserole dish, and a couple of individual casserole dishes. I wanted more stew to biscuit ratio. Then I dropped small biscuits on top and baked for 20 minutes. The biscuits were done, and since I had sauteed the veggies until they were tender, there was no need to cook longer. One tip: make sure to season the stew with salt and pepper before you top it with biscuits, unless you want to let people move their biscuits aside to season it themselves.

text:
Good, but too much basil for my taste.  I cut  the butter down to 1 Tbl. (would do that again!).  I added 1/2 tsp. poultry seasoning, and omitted the sugar (didn't think it needed any sweetness).  Instead of 4 cups broth, I used 3 cups broth + 1 cup milk (skim was fine).  I also used 1/2 of a 12-oz pkg of frozen peas (no need to simmer 5 minutes if they are thawed).  I think next time I will decrease the flour to 1/4 cup - was able to taste the flour with 1/2 cup.  If you follow the recipe on the Bisquick buttermilk baking mix box, it says to use 2 1/4 cups mix  for biscuits with 2/3 cup milk.  I just made them as 'drop' biscuits - too sticky to flatten.  Really was a cross between chicken pot pie & chicken and dumplings!  Thanks for the recipe!
